Jamison Brereton

46 (666)
Indra (1тАУ20), Da╠Дnastuti (21тАУ24), Va╠Дyu (25тАУ28), Da╠Дnastuti (29тАУ33)
Va┼Ыa A┼Ыvya
33 verses: a variety of lyric meters combining 8- and 12- and 4-syllable p─Бdas
This hymn has been called the most metrically varied hymn in the R╠еgveda: it con tains verses of nearly twenty different meters, although all the verses that allow analysis appear to be made up of the standard building blocks of eight-, twelve-, and four-syllable p─Бdas in various combinations. (Some irresolvable irregularities remain.) For the most part, the verses are grouped into two-verse pairs (anomalous prag─Бthas), but the hymn begins with a tr╠еca (vss. 1тАУ3), and the metrically messy verses 14тАУ16 also appear to form a tr╠еca. The two d─Бnastuti sections (vss. 21тАУ24 and 29тАУ33), broken by two prag─Бthas to V─Бyu, show no internal metrical struc ture. The meter is discussed by Oldenberg with his characteristic acuity both in the Prolegomena (1888: 109тАУ10) and in the Noten. The hymn is miscellaneous in content as well. It begins and continues for some time as a fairly standard Indra hymn, insistently focused on begging Indra for gifts of all sorts. The Indra section continues through verse 20, but becomes more and more problematic, with metrical and syntactic difficulties reinforcing each other. Verses 14тАУ16 are metrically almost unanalyzable, and they consist in great part of syntactic fragments the relationships among which are difficult to construct. Verse 17 (paired in a prag─Бtha with 18) equally resists metrical and exegetical certainty, but introduces the Maruts as a counterweight to Indra; in verse 18 we return to more rational metrical structure and, to some degree, analyzable syntax. The last two verses of the Indra section (19тАУ20) are fairly straightforward and bring the praise of Indra to a conclusion with an explosion of adjectives (the first hemistich of 20 is also made entirely of vocatives).
The remaining thirteen verses of the hymn consist of three almost equal parts: two d─Бnastutis (vss. 21тАУ24, 29тАУ33), interrupted by a d─Бnastuti-tinged section addressed to the wind god V─Бyu, who participates in the Morning Pressing, when the priestly gifts are distributed. Both d─Бnastutis mention extravagant numbers of livestock. In the first the poet Va┼Ыa A┼Ыvya mentions himself (vs. 21) and his patron Pr╠еthu┼Ыravas K─Бnita (vss. 21, 24); the final verse (24) of this first d─Бnastuti has a distinctly sum
mary tone and clearly spells out the cause-and-effect relation between gifts and fame. The second d─Бnastuti mentions a more various set of patrons, and the poet names himself in the final verse (33), as a тАЬgreat maiden,тАЭ clearly his favorite gift, is brought toward him. The diction and style of both d─Бnastutis is straightforward; they lack the sly puns and clever insult-as-praise and praise-as-insult that characterize many d─Бnastutis and seem intent only on counting up the spoils. The four intervening verses (25тАУ28) describes V─БyuтАЩs dawn journey to the sacrifice, but it is made clear that his purpose there is to give, or (vs. 27) to motivate the patron to give, to the poet.

Jamison Brereton Notes

English translation:

тАЬIn him abide united all secure protections; lord of vast wealth, may his gliding steeds bear him to theexpressed Soma for his exhilaration.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

All secure protections: a reference to the troops of the Maruts whoaccompany Indra

Jamison Brereton

For in him exist all fearless forms of help altogether.
Let the spans convey him hither, who has many goods; let the fallow bays convey him to the pressed (soma) for exhilaration.

For verily combined in him are all the fearless powers of aid.
Him, rich in wealth, let swift Steeds bring to us, his Bays, to Soma juice for his carouse:

English translation:

тАЬThat exhilaration of your, Indra, which is pre-eminent, which utterly desroys your enemies, which winswealth from men, and is invincible in battles.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

From men: nс╣Ыbhiс╕е = ┼Ыatrubhyaс╕е, from your foes

Your exhilaration, which is worthy to be chosen, which is the most Vr╠еtra-smiting, o Indra,
which with superior men takes the sun, which is difficult to surpass in battlesтАФ с│У

Jamison Brereton Notes

Jamison Brereton Notes

A thematic and syntactic modulation. The y├бс╕е clauses of vs. 8 (which lacks a main clause) clearly refer to IndraтАЩs m├бda- тАШexhilarationтАЩ, and the y├бс╕е which opens vs. 9 seems simply to continue this construction. But the 2nd hemistich is couched in the 2nd ps. and refers to Indra, and it is possible to assume that Indra is also the subject of ab (despite the 3rd ps. construction and the 2nd ps. vocative), because the qualifiers in 9ab are better suited to Indra than to his m├бda-. (As Oldenberg says, тАЬ├Ьbergleiten von Indras m├бda zu I. selbst.тАЭ) In the end, though, it is better to assume a covert identification of Indra and his m├бda-, which allows a smooth transition from describing the latter to describing the former.

With Heroes wins the light of heaven, and is invincible in war:

Jamison Brereton Notes

A thematic and syntactic modulation. The y├бс╕е clauses of vs. 8 (which lacks a main clause) clearly refer to IndraтАЩs m├бda- тАШexhilarationтАЩ, and the y├бс╕е which opens vs. 9 seems simply to continue this construction. But the 2nd hemistich is couched in the 2nd ps. and refers to Indra, and it is possible to assume that Indra is also the subject of ab (despite the 3rd ps. construction and the 2nd ps. vocative), because the qualifiers in 9ab are better suited to Indra than to his m├бda-. (As Oldenberg says, тАЬ├Ьbergleiten von Indras m├бda zu I. selbst.тАЭ) In the end, though, it is better to assume a covert identification of Indra and his m├бda-, which allows a smooth transition from describing the latter to describing the former.

English translation:

тАЬVerily, hero, I find no limit to your wealth; O Maghavan, the thunderer, bestow (your gifts) quickly uponus, and bless our offerings with (abundant) food.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

For I do not find a limit to your generosity in any way, o champion. Show favor to us, bounteous possessor of the stone, even now. You have aided our poetic insights with your prizes.

Griffith

For, Hero, nowhere can I find the bounds of thy munificence.
Still do thou favour us, O Bolt-armed Maghavan: with strength hast thou rewarded hymns.

Geldner

Denn nicht finde ich ├╝berhaupt ein Ende deiner Freigebigkeit, o Held. Sei uns auch ferner gewogen, Gabenreicher, Herr des Pre├Яsteins! Du hast unseren Gedanken durch Belohnungen Wohlwollen bezeigt.

Grassmann

Denn nimmer finde ich, o Held, ein Ende deiner Spendelust; Sei stets, o m├дcht’ger Schleuderer, gewogen uns, durch Gaben lohntest du Gebet.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThe graceful Indra, whose friends extol him, knows, praised of many, all births; him, the mighty, all meninvoke at all times, seizing the ladles (for oblation).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

All men: vi┼Ыve m─Бnuс╣г─Б, all the priests, adhvaryus etc.associated with men, sarvepy adhvary─Бdayo manuс╣гyasambandhinaс╕е

Jamison Brereton

The lofty one who makes his comrade famous, he, praised by many, knows all the races.
Through the human lifespans they all call on him, on Indra the
powerful, with their offering ladles extended.

Griffith

High, glorifier of his friend, he knows all generations, he whom many praise.
All races of mankind with ladies lifted up invoke that Mighty Indra’s aid.

Grassmann

Der seinen Freunden Ruhm verleiht, der vielgelobte, grosse kennt die Wesen all, Die Schale reichend rufen ihn, den starken Indra, aller Menschen St├дmme an.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬAt the time of the exhilaration of the Soma, sing, according to your hymns, with a loud voice, you wisehero Indra, the humbler of enemies, the strong, the ever-worthy to be praised.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Your wise hero: vaс╕е = yuyanr; or,yuс╣гm─Бkam hitay─Б; vaco yath─Б = in the g─Бyatr─л or triс╣гс╣нubh metre;

N─Бma = ┼Ыatr┼лс╣З─Бm n─Бmakam

Jamison Brereton

Sing to the hero amid the raptures of the stalk; with a great hymn (sing) to the discriminating one,
Indra by name, worthy of fame, capable like speech.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes v├бco y├бth─Б as a truncated clause: тАЬsoweit (es) die Rede (vermag),тАЭ but, although accented y├бth─Б is seldom p─Бda-final, unaccented yath─Б, the simile marker, is almost always so placed. Therefore p─Бda-final y├бth─Б here must also be a simile marker at least in my view, but see Oldenberg for contrary opinion.

Griffith

In the wild raptures of the juice sing to your Hero with high laud, to him the Wise,
To Indra, glorious in his name, the Mighty One, even as the hymn alloweth it.

Geldner

Besing euren Helden im Rausche des Trankes mit hoher Rede, den Einsichtsvollen, den Indra, den ber├╝hmten Namen, den M├дchtigen, soweit es die Rede vermag.

Grassmann

Besinge [oder besingen will ich, wenn g─Бy─Б zu lesen] euren Helden bei den Rauschtr├дnken des Soma, den weisen mit erhabenem Liede, Indra mit Namen den ber├╝hmten, im wahren Sinne des Wortes kr├дftigen.

English translation:

тАЬ(Indra), invoked by many, speedily give me wealth; give riches, give abundance of food in battle.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Speedily: atha = adya

Jamison Brereton

(You are by nature) one who gives a legacy to the body [=a son], who gives goods, who gives a prizewinner in the prize-contests, o much invoked oneтАФ
now then (do so)!

Jamison Brereton Notes

Very condensed expression. The first two long p─Бdas characterize Indra as a giver (dad├н- 3x) of various desirable things. The third p─Бda, a mere four syllables, implicitly calls on Indra to actualize this identity by making the gifts.

The expression тАЬlegacy to/for the body/selfтАЭ (r├йkс╣Зas tanv├и) probably stands for a son, as Geldner points out in his n.

The short final p─Бda n┼лn├бm ├бtha is curiously formed. There are no other examples of this word sequence, but n┼лn├бm has a tendency to be followed by a di- or trisyllable beginining with a- (though usually heavy syl), e.g., n┼лn├бm a┼Ыy─Бс╕е, n┼лn├бm any─Б╠Б. Moreover, ├бtha is almost always initial in p─Бda or clause, so its presence in this position must be signalling something special, which I take to be a peremptory command (English тАЬnow then!тАЭ corresponds nicely). Note that it echoes verse-final y├бth─Б of 14 and that it again takes final position at the end of 16.

Griffith

Thou givest wealth to me myself, thou givest treasure, Excellent! and the strong steed,
O Much-invoked, in deeds of might, yea, even now.

Geldner

Du schenkst dem Leib ein Erbe, du schenkst Gut, du schenkst in den K├дmpfen, Vielgerufener, ein siegreiches Ro├Я, auch jetzt.

Grassmann

Der du Reichthum gibst mir selbst, Gut gibst in den Wettk├дmpfen, o vielgerufener, ein schnelles Ross gibst, auch jetzt f├╝rwahr.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬ(We praise you), the lord of all riches, the subduer of this obstructor waging (attacks), – speedily giveus abundant (wealth).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Abundant: atyatha = ady─Бpi, apy─Бdya

Jamison Brereton

(Sing to him) who has control of all goods, who also, when he is victorious, has control of this form (of his?),
(and has control) over those who yearn (for him). Now then!

Jamison Brereton Notes

Following Oldenberg, I supply the verb тАЬsing toтАЭ (abh├н тАж g─Бya) from 14 to govern the accusatives here.

In the published translation I also followed a suggestion of Oldenberg in taking kс╣Ыpayat├бс╕е as acc. pl. governed by ├бti, rather than gen. sg. dependent on v├бrpasaс╕е (Geldner: тАЬ├╝ber diese Gestalt des ErbarmendenтАЭ). But the syntactic distribution of elements in this verse is very uncertain, due in part to the unclarity of the meter, where even p─Бda boundaries cannot be certainly determined. In coming to the version found in the publ tr. I reasoned that what confronts us here is a sort of syntactic ┼Ыleс╣гa of irajy├бnt-, with the uncompounded participle as usual governing the genitive in p─Бdas a and b (v├н┼Ыveс╣г─Бm тАж v├бs┼лn─Бm and asy├б v├бrpasaс╕е), while with ├бti in p─Бda c it takes the accusative. Cf., with тИЪr─Бj, a root with which irajy├б- becomes entangled, III.10.7 v├н r─Бjasi ├бti sr├нdhaс╕е.

I am now not so certain: I think kс╣Ыpayat├бс╕е may in fact be a gen. as Geldner takes it, but that itтАЩs construed directly with irajy├бnt-, not dependent on v├бrpasaс╕е – with the tr.

тАЬ(and has control) over the one who yearns (for him) in addition.тАЭ Under this interpr.

├бti would be an adverbial additive тАШin additionтАЩ, adding another term to the items over which Indra has control.

What тАЬthis formтАЭ refers to is not clear to me. I assume that it is IndraтАЩs form, quite possibly one of the multiforms that he takes on at will Since n┼лn├бm тАж ├бtha reprises 15c, I find the interpolation of the ├бti puzzling, especially if it governs a previous nominal form. However, the poet (who seems to have little conscience about syntax) may have inserted ├бti here because ├бti[y]├бtha would echo the y├бth─Б that ends vs. 14.

Griffith

Him, Sovran Ruler of all precious things, who even hath power o’er this fair form of his,
As now it taketh shape, and afterward,

Der ├╝ber alle Sch├дtze verf├╝gt und auch wenn er Sieger ist, ├╝ber diese Gestalt des Erbarmenden verf├╝gt, jetzt und auch ferner.

Der ├╝ber alle G├╝ter verf├╝gt, der Gewalt hat auch ├╝ber jene Truggestalt, die sich jetzt ├╝ber die Geb├╝hr breit macht.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬI desire the coming of you, the mighty one, we give praise with oblations and ymns to the showerer whohastens readily (to the sacrifice), associated with the Maruts, you are worshipped of all men; I glorify you withadoration and praise.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

We shall praise you great ones [=Maruts] for the rewarder fit for nourishment, who comes fittingly, who comes regularly [=Indra]. Through the sacrifices and the hymns of all the peoples of Manu, you [=Indra] are likely to attain (the favor) of the Maruts.
I sing to you reverently with a hymn.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Another very disturbed verse. My interpretation follows Oldenberg in great degree, but with crucial deviations.

In the first p─Бda I read, with Grassmann, Oldenberg, and Scarlatta (61), a compound ├бram-iс╣гe, rather than two separate words with Geldner (also Pp.; cf. Lubotsky p. 321 s.v. iс╣гe), who is forced to take this as a parenthetical 1st ps. declaration (тАЬich beeile mich rechtтАЭ). This compound qualifies Indra in the dative and matches araс╣Гgam─Б╠Бya in b quite nicely. The accent on the verb st├бv─Бmahe can be accounted for (in a somewhat ad hoc fashion) as Oldenberg does, as a separate four-syllable p─Бda, following an eight-syllable opening.

In de (if this is the correct division), I take gen. pl. vi┼Ыv├бmanuс╣г─Бm with yaj├▒├йbhir g─лrbh├нс╕е тАЬthrough the sacrifices and the hymns of all the peoples of Manu.тАЭ This has the somewhat awkward consequence of separating it from the immediately following gen. pl. mar├║t─Бm, though if the p─Бda break follows vi┼Ыv├бmanuс╣г─Бс╣Г rather than g─лrbh├нс╕е as Oldenberg takes it, the syntactic separation would be less problematic. (This would produce a p─Бda of 10 or 11 syllables [with distraction of -manuс╣гa─Бm], followed by one of 8 syllables [also with distraction of gen. pl. -─Бm].) Geldner takes the subject of iyakс╣гasi to be the poet addressing himself, while I think that it is Indra, who is the subject of the same verb in the immediately preceding hymn (VIII.45.31). The question then is what the object is. Geldner supplies the pronoun тАЬdies,тАЭ but the referent of this pronoun isnтАЩt clear to me. I suggest rather sumn├бm тАШfavorтАЩ: the stem ├нyakс╣гa- several times takes sumn├бm as object (I.153.2, II.20.1. X.50.3), and it appears here in the next verse (18d), where I supply this verb.

If this assumption is correct, we must then ask why Indra would seek to attain the favor of the Maruts. The key to that is probably the odd snatch of dialogue in the last hymn (VIII.45.37-38), in which Indra complains that the Maruts deserted him in his time of need; here he seeks their good will as support in the Vс╣Ыtra battle.

Griffith

We praise, so that the Mighty One may speed to you, Pourer of boun ies, Traveller, prepared to go.
Thou favourest the Maruts known to all, by song and sacrifice.
With song and praise I sing to thee.

Euch, die gro├Яen Marut - ich beeile mich recht, - loben wir fein vor dem freigebigen, gern kommenden, oft sich einstellenden Indra, - mit Opfern und Lobreden auf die allen Menschen bekannten Marut suchst du dies zu erreichen, - ich besinge dich unter Verbeugung mit Lobeswort.

Grassmann

Sehr hoch preisen wir euren zur H├╝lfe herbeieilenden, gn├дdigen, h├╝lfreichen, kommenden, mit Opfern und Liedern strebst du nach den allen Menschen angeh├╢rigen Maruts; ich singe dir anbetungsvoll mit meinem Liede.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(We present) the oblation to those loud-sounding (Maruts) who rush along with the streaming trains ofthe clouds; may we obtain in the sacrifice the happiness which those deep-roarers bestow.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Streaming trains:ajman = gamanam (RV 1.166.5), saс╣Еgr─Бma (RV 1.112.17); here, balair balakarair udakaiс╕е

Jamison Brereton

Those who launch themselves in flight on their drives along the backs of the mountainsтАФ
the sacrifice of those greatly noisy ones, the favor of those powerfully noisy ones (you are likely to attain) while the ceremony is pro(ceeding).

Jamison Brereton Notes

The referents of the plurals in this verse continue to be the Maruts of the previous verse, and I think that the same situation obtains: Indra is seeking the sacrifice and favor of the Maruts. I therefore supply iyakс╣гasi in this verse, again with sumn├бm as object. Thus one half of the VP is found in each verse: iyakс╣гasi in 17, sumn├бm in 18. (Geldner also supplies the same verb stem, but in the 1st sg., referring to the poet.) The medial transitive-causative p─Бt├бyante I take as a reflexive: тАШcause themselves to fly, launch themselves in flightтАЩ.

On the pseudo-loc. absol. pr─Б╠Бdhvar├й see comm. ad VIII.12.31-33.

Griffith

We in the sacrifice perform their will whose voice is lifted high,
The worship of those Thundering Ories who o’er the ridges of these mountains fly in troops.

Geldner

Die sich mit ihren Schw├дrmen ├╝ber die R├╝cken der Berge st├╝rzen, dieser lautbrausenden Opfer, die Gunst der heftig Brausenden m├╢chte ich bei dem Gottesdienst erreichen.

Grassmann

Die in ihren Z├╝gen ├╝ber der Berge Gipfel fliegen, der sehr brausenden Verehrung, der laut brausenden Preis stell’ ich voran beim Opferfest.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬ(We worship) the crusher of the malevolent, most powerful Indra, bring to us suitable wealth, Oinspirer– (bring) most excellent( wealth), O inspirer.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

O inspirer: codayanmate = dhanam prerayanti matir yasya,you whose mind sends wealth to his worshipper; in RV 5.86.6, it is applied to the eye, ‘having the mind as itsinstigator

Jamison Brereton

O strongest Indra, bring here the shatterer of bad thoughts,
(namely) wealth to be harnessed for us, o you who stir thoughtтАФ
preeminent (wealth), o you who stir thought.

Jamison Brereton Notes

For wealth as a тАШshattererтАЩ (prabhaс╣Еg├б-), see VI.68.3 where it is the implied subject of pr├б тАж bhan├бkti.

Griffith

O Indra, Mightiest, bring us that which crushes men of evil minds,
Wealth suited to our needs, O Stirrer of the thought, best wealth, O thou who stirrest thought.

Geldner

Bring den uns geb├╝hrenden Reichtum, gewaltigster Indra, der alle Bosheiten bricht, du Gedankenanreger, den vorz├╝glichsten, du Gedankenanregendster,

Grassmann

Den Zerbrecher der b├╢segesinnten, o st├дrkster Indra, bringe herbei, den uns geb├╝hrenden Reichthum, o Sinnerreger, den trefflichsten, o Sinnerreger.

Elizarenkova

рд╣реЗ рд╕рдирд┐рддрдГ рд╕рдВрднрдХреНрддрд░реНрджрд╛рддрд░реНрд╡рд╛ рдЙрдЧреНрд░ рдЙрджреНрдЧреВрд░реНрдгрдмрд▓ рдЪрд┐рддреНрд░ рдЪрд╛рдпрдиреАрдп рдЪреЗрддрд┐рд╖реНрда рдЕрддреНрдпрдиреНрддрдВ рдЪреЗрддрдпрд┐рддрдГ рд╕реВрдиреГрдд рд╕реБрд╕рддреНрдп рдкреНрд░рд╛рд╕рд╣рд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╕рд╣реНрдп рд╣реЗ рд╕рдореНрд░рд╛рдЯреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╕реНрдп рд╕реНрд╡рд╛рдорд┐рдиреН рд╕рдореНрдпрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдЬрдорд╛рди рд╡рд╛ рддреНрд╡рдВ рд╕рд╣реБрд░рд┐рдВ рд╕рд╣рдирд╢реАрд▓рдВ рднреБрдЬреНрдпреБрдВ рднреЛрдЬрдпрд┐рддрд╛рд░рдВ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡реНрдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡реГрджреНрдзрдореН ред рдореБрдЦреНрдпрдорд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдИрджреГрд╢рдВ рдзрдирдВ рд╡рд╛рдЬреЗрд╖реБ рд╕рдВрдЧреНрд░рд╛рдореЗрд╖реНрд╡рд╛рднрд░реЗрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд╖рдГ рее рее рек рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬO bountiful, mos bountiful, mighty, wondeful, best giver of knowledge and supremely truthful, by yourprowess, universal ruler, (bring to us) in conflicts ample wealth, overpowering those who attack us, and causingenjoyment.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Bhujyam, p┼лrvyam: two epithes applied in RV 8.22.2 to the chariot of the A┼Ыvins;

P┼лrvya = goingbefore (in battle);

Bhujyu = preserver of all

Jamison Brereton

O winner, good winner, powerful, brilliant, most brilliant, liberal-spirited, sovereign king, (bring wealth) victorious through victory,
victory-winning, enjoyable, foremost at the prize-contests.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the full hemistich of vocatives, all accented because there is no inherently tonic word to follow.

As Oldenberg points out, all the accusatives of the second hemistich should be grouped with ray├нm in 19, and the verb of that verse ─Б╠Бbhara continues to have domain over this one.

Griffith

O Winner, noble winner, strong, wondrous, most splendid, excellent,
Sole Lord of victory, bring all-ovcrpowering wealth, joy-giving, chief in deeds of might.

Geldner

Du Gewinner, t├╝chtiger Gewinner, Gewaltiger, Ausgezeichneter, Ausgezeichnetster, Gro├Яm├╝tiger, du Allherrscher, durch ├Ьbermacht gewaltigen, ├╝berw├дltigenden, genu├Яbietenden, der bei den Preisk├дmpfen der Vorderste ist!

Grassmann

O [Spender] sch├╢nspendender, gewaltiger [gl├дnzender] hellgl├дnzendster, herrlicher, mit Allgewallt, o Oberherr, machtest du siegreich den [siegenden] Bhudschju, der in den K├дmpfen der erste ist.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрддреНрд░ рд╢реМрдирдХрдГ-тАШрд╡рд╢рд╛рдпрд╛рд╢реНрд╡реНрдпрд╛рдп рдпрддреНрдкреНрд░рд╛рджрд╛рддреНрдХрд╛рдиреАрддрд╕реНрддреБ рдкреГрдереБрд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╛рдГ ред рддрджрддреНрд░ рд╕реНрддреВрдпрддреЗ рджрд╛рдирдорд╛ рд╕ рдПрддреНрд╡реЗрд╡рдорд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рдГ’ (рдмреГрд╣рджреНрджреЗ рем.ренреп-реореж)ред рдПрддреБ рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреБ рд╕рдГ рдпрдГ рдЕрджреЗрд╡рдГ рджреЗрд╡рд╛рджрдиреНрдпреЛ рдордиреБрд╖реНрдпреЛ рд╡рд╢рдГ рдИрд╡рддреН рдЧрдордирд╡рддреН рдЧрд╡рд╛рджрд┐рд▓рдХреНрд╖рдгрдВ рдкреВрд░реНрддрдВ рдкреВрд░реНрдгрдореН рдЖрджрджреЗ рдЖрджрддреНрддреЗ ред рд╕реНрд╡реАрдХреГрддрд╡рд╛рдирд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рджреЗрд╡рд╢реНрдЪреЗрдиреНрдорд╛рдпрдпрд╛рдкреНрдпрд╛рдЧрдиреНрддреБрдорд░реНрд╣рддрд┐ ред рдЕрддрдГ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢реЗрдиреИрд╡рд╛рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддреНрд╡рд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдХрдердорд╕реНрдп рдзрдирд╛рд╡рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рдкреНрд░рд╕рдЩреНрдЧ рдЖрдЧрдордирдкреНрд░рд╕рдЩреНрдЧрд╢реНрдЪреЗрддрд┐ рддрджреБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдпрдерд╛ рдЪрд┐рддреН ред рдЪрд┐рджрд┐рддрд┐ рдкреВрд░рдгрдГ ред рдпреЗрди рдХрд╛рд░рдгреЗрди рдпрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреНрд╡рд╛ рд╡рд╢рдГ рдПрддрддреНрд╕рдВрдЬреНрдЮрдХрдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡реНрдпрдГ рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рдкреБрддреНрд░рдГ рдкреГрдереБрд╢реНрд░рд╡рд╕рд┐ рдПрддрдиреНрдирд╛рдордХреЗ рд░рд╛рдЬреНрдЮрд┐ рдХрд╛рдиреАрддреЗ рдХрдиреАрддрдкреБрддреНрд░реЗ рдХрдиреНрдпрд╛рдпрд╛рдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░реЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдЙрд╖рд╕рдГ рд╡реНрдпреБрд╖рд┐ рд╡реНрдпреБрд╖реНрдЯреМ рдЖрджрджреЗ рдЖрджрддреНрддреЗ рддреЗрди рдХрд╛рд░рдгреЗрди рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рджреНрд╡рд╛ рдХрд╛рд░рдгрд╛рджрд╛рдпрд╛рддреНрд╡рд┐рддрд┐ ред рдПрд╡рдорд╢реНрд╡реЛ рдмрдиреНрдзреБрд╡рд░реНрдЧреЛ рд╡рд╛ рдмреНрд░реВрддреЗ рее

тАЬLet him draw near, who, though not a god, would receive this complete living gift– since Va┼Ыa, the sonof A┼Ыva, receives it at the dawn of this (morning) at the hands of Pс╣Ыthu┼Ыravas, the son of K─Бn─лta.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ivat = gamanavad, gav─Бdilakс╣гaс╣Зam;

P┼лrtam = p┼лrс╣Зam; or, ivat = iyat, such,so great; or, p┼лrtam = pious works;

K─Бn─лta: son of a maiden, kany─Бy─Бс╕е putraс╕е

English translation:

тАЬI have received sixty thousand horses, and ens of housands– a score of hundreds of camels– athousand brown mares– and ten times ten thousand cows with three red patches.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Three red patches: i.e. havingthe head, back, and sides white (or bright); the с╣Ыca and the next two с╣Ыcas are spoken by Va┼Ыa

I have won sixty thousands in equine property, myriads, twenty
hundreds of camels,
ten hundreds of dusky mares, ten of those with three red spots, ten
thousands of cows.

Steeds sixty thousand and ten thousand kine, and twenty hundred camels I obtained;
Ten hundred brown in hue, and other ten red in three spots: in all, ten thousand kine.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬTen brown horses bear along the wheel (of my chariot), of mature vigour, of complete power, andtrampling down obstacles.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Of complee power: v─лtav─Бr─Бsaс╕е = kr─Бntabalaс╕е pr─Бptabala v─Б, having sleektails

Jamison Brereton

Ten dusky (stallions), following wealth to fulfillment,
straight-tailed, swift,
skittish, have turned the felly homeward.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On с╣Ыdh├бd-r─л/i- see Thieme 1958 (Fs. Turner): 157, EWA 118 (s.v. ARDH). Thieme tr. тАШluckily reaching wealthтАЩ. The nearby passage VIII.48.2 ┼Ыra├║с╣гс╣н─лva dh├║ram ├бnu r─Бy├б rdhy ╠е ─Бс╕е seems to confirm a connection between -r─л/i and ray├н. I tr. 48.2 тАЬlike an obedient mare the chariot pole you should follow riches to fulfillmentтАЭ and adopt that interpretation here.

Their tails are presumably straight because they are going so fast their tails are horizontal.

Geldner takes mathr├б- as a geographical designation: Mathra horses. But I see no reason not to connect it with тИЪmath тАШchurn, agitateтАЩ, hence тАШskittishтАЩ. See also I.181.5.

Griffith

Ten browns that make my wealth increase, fleet steeds whose tails are long and fair,
Turn with swift whirl my chariot wheel;

Geldner

Zehn dunkelbraune Matharosse, den Lauf gewinnende Renner mit geradem Schweife, wendeten im Kreise um,

Grassmann

Zehn schnelle Rappen des Ridhadr─л mit langgestreckten Schw├дnzen drehten rollend den Radkranz um.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬThese arehtje gifts of the wealthy Pс╣Ыthu┼Ыravas, the son of K─Бn─лta; he, bestowing a golden chariot,has proved himself most liberal and wise, he has won most abundant fame.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

These are the gifts of Pr╠еthu┼Ыravas K─Бnita, the very generous.
In giving a golden chariot, he has become the most bounteous patron. He has made his fame the highest.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The final p─Бda contains a pun on the patronтАЩs name Pс╣Ыthu┼Ыravas. See Watkins 1995: 73-74.

Griffith

The gifts which Prthusravas gave, Kanita’s son munificent.
He gave a chariot wrought of gold: the prince was passing bountiful, and won himself most lofty fame.

Geldner

Die Geschenke des freigebigen Prithusravas, des Kanitasohnes. Indem er einen goldenen Wagen schenkte, ist er der freigebigste Lohnherr geworden; er hat sich h├╢chsten Ruhm erworben.

Grassmann

Die Gaben des Prithu├зravas K─Бn─лta sind sehr reichlich, einen goldenen Wagen schenkend hat sich der F├╝rst seh freigiebig gezeigt und h├╢chsten Ruhm erlangt.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬCome to us, V─Бyu, to bestow great wealth and glorious strength; we have offered (libations) to you thegiver of abundant (wealth), we have offered immediately to you the giver of great (gifts).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

V─Бyu, drive here to us for the extension and the spread (of our line) to be great and for bounty.
For we have performed (a sacrifice) for you, for you to give much, to give greatly all at once.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take t├бne and p─Б╠Бjase as complementary concepts, vertical and horizontal - our descendants and our synchronic extension.

Griffith

Come thou to this great rite of ours, Vayu! to give us vigorous light.
We have served thee that thou mightest give much to us, yea, mightest quickly give great wealth.

Geldner

Komm zu uns, Vayu, zu gro├Яer Lebensdauer, zur Freigebigkeit und zu leibhaftiger Erscheinung, denn wir haben dir ein Opfer bereitet, da├Я du viel schenkest, da├Я du sofort t├╝chtig schenkest.

Grassmann

Komm her zu langer Dauer uns, dem K├дmpfer, Vaju, recht zur Kraft, Wir dienten dir, damit du viel uns schenken sollst, recht grosses du uns schenken sollst.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe who is borne on horses and surrounds himself with thrice seven times seventy cows– he comes toyou with these Soma-libations and Soma-priests, to offer to you, drinker of the Soma, drinker of the bright pureSoma.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

He = Pс╣Ыthu┼Ыravas

Jamison Brereton

As the one who drives here with his horses at the breaking of the dayтАФ with the thrice seven seventiesтАФ
(invigorated) with these soma drinks by the soma-pressers, (be ready) to give, you soma-drinker, drinker of the clear purified (soma).

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse gives the impression of being constructed from random constituents, although some cohesion can be wrested from it.

Following Oldenberg I take b as further specifying the horses in a (├б┼Ыvebhiс╕е), with the bare numeral sapt├б substituting for the non-existent instrumental *sapt├бbhiс╕е as elsewhere. It could also specify the number of soma drinks in c (s├│mebhiс╕е), and the position of the phrase between those two instrumental expressions allows it to be construed with both. The gen. pl. saptat─лn─Б╠Бm of course simply depends on the numeral.

In c I supply a form of тИЪmad/mand to be construed with the instr.; so also Geldner (ermuntert).

In d I supply a form such as maс╣Гhase тАШyou are readyтАЩ, which is common with d─Бn─Б╠Бya, although GeldnerтАЩs solution, to have the infinitive depend only on the тАЬermuntertтАЭ is certainly possible and probably neater. See also Scarlatta 313.

Griffith

Who with thrice seven times seventy horses comes to us, invested with the rays of morn,
Through these our Soma-draughts and those who press, to give, drinker of pure bright Soma Juice.

Geldner

Der in der Morgend├дmmerung mit Rossen gefahren kommt als Schenker von dreimal sieben mal siebenzig K├╝hen von diesen Somapressern mit Soma zum Schenken ermuntert, du Somatrinker, der du den hellen Kl├дrtrank trinkst.

Grassmann

Er f├дhrt mit Rossen dreimal sieb’nmal siebzigen und schm├╝ckt die Morgenr├╢then aus, Zur Gab’ gestimmt durch Soma’s und die Presser hier, o der du reinen Soma trinkst.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬHe who of his own will has been plural ased to give me this honoured gift, he, performer of good works,(has determined) on a pre-eminently good action, amid Aratva, Nahuс╣гa and Sukс╣Ыtvan.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Maybe, names of kingsor officers of Pс╣Ыthu┼Ыravas

Jamison Brereton

The one of good resolve who by his breath invigorated just this man here, to give something brilliant to me
in the axle made of araс╣нu wood, in the presence of Nahuс╣гa, who is a good performer (of rituals) for (a god) who performs even better,

Jamison Brereton Notes

Another verse with unclear referents and no main clause. I take the subject to be the god V─Бyu, who has inspired the human patron (im├бm in a) to give the poet a splendid dakс╣гiс╣З─Б. If V─Бyu (deified wind) is the subject, tm├бn─Б lit. тАШby his breathтАЩ is a nice touch.

In c Geldner takes araс╣нv├й ├бkс╣гe as a PN, and it is certainly tempting. But, although the second part of that p─Бda is a PN, interpreting all difficult phrases as names is a practice to be avoided, and Mayrhofer (EWA s.v. araс╣нv├б-; also PN s.v.) rejects the name interpretation in favor of тАЬaus dem Holz der araс╣нu-BaumesтАЭ (Wagenachse).

There is no way to be certain.

Griffith

Who hath inclined this glorious one, buunteous himself, to give me gifts.
Borne on firm chariot with the prosperous Nahup, wise, to a man yet more devout.

Geldner

Der sogar diesen in eigener Person begeisterte, mir Wunderbares zu schenken, bei Aratva Aksa, dem frommen Nahusa, der Weise dem am besten Opfernden;

Grassmann

Der diesen Herrn begeisterte, um Herrliches zu schenken mir, Auf festem Wagen bei dem treuen Nahuscha, treu wirkend f├╝r den treueren.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe who is self-resplendent in his glorious body, who is bright, O V─Бyu, like gh─л, has given me thisfood, brought by horses, brought by camels, brought by dogs.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Self-resplendent: he who is lord over (the kings)uchathya and vapus; brought by camels: rajas = a camel or as ass

Jamison Brereton

You who are an independent king, in a wondrous form worthy of praise and bathed in ghee, o V─БyuтАФ
this drive (of yours), horse-impelled, dust-impelled, dog-impelled,
pro(ceeds). Here it is now!

Jamison Brereton Notes

Another virtually impenetrable verse. Rather than discuss my deviations from othersтАЩ interpretations, I will just set out the considerations that produced my own translation.

I take the referent of the y├бс╕е in the relative clauses that dominate vss. 26-28 to be V─Бyu in all cases. In this verse thereтАЩs the embarrassment of the voc. v─Бyo, but since there is no verb in 28 nothing prevents it from being couched in the 2nd sg. The ut├б in b I take as connecting ucathy├и v├бpuс╣гi and ghr╠еtasn─Б╠Бс╕е, both used of the svar─Б╠Бс╣н, despite their different cases.

I think cd represents a new clause, with implied тАЬyourтАЭ; the pr─Б╠Бjma is rather like pr─Б╠Бdhvar├й in 18, with verb extruded from the pr├б. The last little bit, id├бm n├║ t├бt, is a separate clause (like n┼лn├бm [├бty] ├бtha in 15-16).

Griffith

Sole Lord in beauty meet for praise, O Vayu, dropping fatness down,
Hurried along by steeds, by camels, and by hounds, spreads forth thy train: even this it is.

Geldner

Und der der Selbstherrscher in preisw├╝rdiger Gestalt ist, o Vayu, mit Schmalz gebadet. Von Rossen getrieben, von Staub getrieben, vom Hund getrieben bewegt sich jetzt dieser Zug vorw├дrts.

Grassmann

Die fettbedeckt und leuchtend ist, o Vaju, herrlich von Gestalt, Bespannt mit Rossen, Antilopen, Hunden auch, dringt vor die Schar, schon ist sie hier.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬI have now received (a gift) dear to the beneficent king, sixty thousand bulls vigorous like horses.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Now then, I have won something dear to the vigorous one, sixty thousand
(geldings, which are) just like stallions.

Jamison Brereton Notes

After the puzzling detour into V─Бyu, this verse reunites us with the d─Бnastuti of vss. 21-24 by means of asanam тАШI wonтАЩ in b, found also in 22a.

тАЬGeldingтАЭ is supplied on the basis of vs. 20.

Griffith

So, as a prize dear to the strong, the sixty thousand have I gained,
Bulls that resemble vigorous steeds.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬSince, when the herd were wandering (to the wood), he called a hundred camels (to give them to me),and two thousand from among the white herds (of cows).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Then when in a roving band [=caravan] a hundred camels roared, then (I took) twenty hundreds from the ┼Ъvitnas.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I supply ─Б╠Бdade from 32b, though asanam from 29a would also be possible.

And in the grazing herd he made a hundred camels bleat for me,
And twenty hundred mid the white.
